TI Theory of multipolar excitations in CeB6
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
DE antiferro-quadrupolar order; multipolar excitations; CeB6
AB A theory for the multipolar excitations in the antiferro-quadrupolar (AFQ) phase of CeB6 is developed. It is based on a pseudo-spin model for the Gamma(8) ground state of Ce used previously to explain the B-T phase diagram. An equation of motion method for the multipolar operators is employed and the solutions for the O-2(0) and Oxy phases are given. It is shown that the excitation branches are classified as being of mixed quadrupolar-dipolar, quadrupolar-octupolar and octupolar-dipolar character. The former two have strong and the latter only weak dispersion respectively. The transition from the O-2(0) to the O-xy phase in the symmetric model is accompanied by the reappearance of a quadrupolar Goldstone mode. In the O-xy phase of the asymmetric model some modes are gapped already at zero field and for finite field no Goldstone mode remains. In addition we give a derivation for the dynamical structure function based on the mixing scheme of multipolar excitations and discuss the result for the zero-field case.

TI Interplay of field-induced multipoles in CeB6
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
DE quadrupolar ordering; octupolar moment; multipolar moment; CeB6
AB We propose a theory of CeB6 in a magnetic field by extending and slightly modifying a previous paper. The antiferro-quadrupolar ordering induces dipoles and octupoles when the magnetic field is applied. The nature of those field-induced multipoles is studied by changing the direction of the field. It is shown that the contradiction between NMR and neutron diffraction is resolved by taking into account the influence of octupoles. Thus it is concluded that CeB6 is the first example in which the octupoles play a crucial role on the anomalous f-electron ordered phase.

TI Temperature dependence of optical conductivity in double-exchange
   ferromagnet La(1-x)Sr(x)MnO(3)
SO PHYSICAL REVIEW B
LA English
DT Article
AB The optical absorption observed in ferromagnetic metal La(1-x)Sr(x)MnO(3) shows a strong temperature dependence. Assuming that the temperature dependence comes mainly from the spontaneous magnetization, we study theoretically how the optical conductivity is affected by the decrease of spontaneous magnetization. The coherent-potential approximation is used to describe the effect of t(2g) pin disorder on the optical conductivity, which consists of intraband and interband transitions within e(g) bands. The result explains well some important features of the experimental data.

TI Magnetic-field effects on quadrupolar ordering in CeB6
SO JOURNAL OF MAGNETISM AND MAGNETIC MATERIALS
LA English
DT Article; Proceedings Paper
CT International Conference on Magnetism
CY JUL 27-AUG 01, 1997
CL CAIRNS, AUSTRALIA
DE dense Kondo system; quadrupolar ordering
AB A theory of the antiferro-quadrupolar ordering in CeB6 is developed in the frame-work of the Gamma(8)-quartet basis. Possible ordered phases under the external magnetic field are classified in terms of their symmetry properties. Using a mean-held approximation based on the group theory, the stable quadrupolar phases are investigated for several intersite interactions of all the multipoles. (C) 1998 Elsevier Science B.V. TI Magnetic ordering, orbital state and lattice distortion in perovskite
   manganites
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
DE transition-metal oxide; magnetic ordering; orbital state
ID MAGNETORESISTANCE; LA1-XSRXMNO3; OXIDES; SPIN
AB Possible ordered phases in perovskite manganites are investigated in the framework of an effective spin Hamiltonian for the atomic limit. Using the mean-field approximation combined with a group-theoretical consideration, we determine the stable orbital and spin ordered phases at finite temperatures. It is found that the magnetic ordering with low-symmetry spatial arrangement is stabilized due to the mixing interaction between different multipoles. The resulting orbital states are discussed by taking into account the effect of lattice distortion from the cubic symmetry. The spin and orbital states in LaMnO3 are discussed on the basis of the present theory.

TI Spectral functions of the one-dimensional Hubbard model in the
   U->+infinity limit: How to use the factorized wave function
SO PHYSICAL REVIEW B
LA English
DT Article
ID LUTTINGER-LIQUID BEHAVIOR; CHARGE-SPIN SEPARATION; T-J MODEL; MOMENTUM
   DISTRIBUTION; MAGNETIC-FIELD; PHOTOEMISSION SPECTROSCOPY;
   CONFORMAL-INVARIANCE; CRITICAL EXPONENTS; OPERATOR CONTENT; FERMI GAS
AB We give the details of the calculation of the spectral functions of the one-dimensional Hubbard model using the spin-charge factorized wave function for several versions of the U --> + infinity limit. The spectral functions are expressed as a convolution of charge and spin dynamical correlation functions. A procedure to evaluate these correlation functions very accurately for large systems is developed, and analytical results are presented for the low-energy region. These results are fully consistent with the conformal field theory. We also propose a direct method of extracting the exponents from the matrix elements in more general cases.

TI Magnetic-field effects on quadrupolar ordering in a Gamma(8)-quartet
   system CeB6
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
DE dense Kondo system; CeB6; quadrupolar ordering
ID DENSE KONDO COMPOUNDS; CE0.5LA0.5B6
AB A theory of the antiferro-quadrupolar ordering in CeB6 is developed in the framework of the Gamma(8)-quartet basis. Possible ordered phases under the external magnetic field are classified in terms of their symmetry properties, and the relations between quadrupolar order parameters and field-induced moments are established. Then we formulate a mean-field theory of Ohkawa's RKKY model based on the group-theoretical consideration. The stability of the possible phases and the resulting phase diagrams are analyzed in connection with the character of quadrupolar moments, the influence of induced moments and the form of Zeeman term. Considering available experimental results, we introduce an improved model with asymmetric interactions and discuss the phase diagram of CeB6. The connection between magnetostriction and uniform quadrupolar moments is discussed.

TI Stability of non-Fermi liquid in Kondo effect due to (5f)(2)
   configuration
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
DE Kondo effect; Fermi liquid; non-Fermi liquid; numerical renormalization
   group method
ID RENORMALIZATION-GROUP; CONDUCTION ELECTRONS; MODEL; BEHAVIOR; CHANNEL;
   ANISOTROPY; IMPURITIES; FIELD
AB The stability of the non-Fermi liquid (NFL) in Kondo effect is studied by considering the excited states of the 5f-electrons. First, in order to examine their effects in the strong correlation limit, the exchange model is derived for a tetragonal crystal field by restricting the localized states in f(2) to a non-Kramers doublet and a singlet; all the states are taken into account for f(2). The numerical renormalization group analysis for this model shows that the singlet state in f(2) and one of the excited states in f(1) play an important role to stabilize the Fermi liquid (FL) over the NFL. Second, the same problem is examined for the six-fold orbitally degenerate Anderson model by considering all the local excited states. The competition between FL and NFL sensitively depends on the Coulomb and Hund couplings, the orbital anisotropy and the hybridization term. The six-fold orbital degeneracy is also important to realize NFL; in fact a similar analysis on the four-fold orbitally degenerate Anderson model does not lead to NFL.

TI A new type of fermi-liquid fixed point in kondo effect due to (5f)(2)
   configuration
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
DE Kondo effect; numerical renormalization group method; Fermi liquid;
   non-Fermi liquid
ID RENORMALIZATION-GROUP; CONDUCTION ELECTRONS; FIELD; MODEL
AB The Kondo effect due to (5f)(2) impurities is studied by restricting the S-electron states to a non-Kramers doublet and a singlet in a tetragonal or hexagonal crystal field. The singlet level plays an important role to stabilize the Fermi liquid over the non-Fermi liquid. The nature of the Fermi-liquid fixed point, which results from the numerical renormalization group calculation, is analyzed. It has turned out to be different from the standard one because of a combined effect of two types of local singlets. One is due to the crystal field and the other is due to the Kondo effect. The leading irrelevant interaction near the fixed point is of the Coulomb type, whose couplings depend on the orbital channels of conduction electrons.

TI Shadow band in the one-dimensional infinite-U Hubbard model
SO PHYSICAL REVIEW LETTERS
LA English
DT Article
ID T-J MODEL; TOMONAGA-LUTTINGER MODEL; CHARGE-SPIN SEPARATION; MOMENTUM
   DISTRIBUTION; SPECTRAL PROPERTIES; WAVE-FUNCTION; FERMI GAS;
   TEMPERATURE; EXCITATIONS; EXTENSION
AB We show that the factorized wave function of Ogata and Shiba can be used to calculate the k dependent spectral functions of the one-dimensional, infinite-U Hubbard model, and of some extensions to finite U. The resulting spectral function is remarkably rich: In addition to low energy features typical of Luttinger liquids, there is a well defined band, which we identify as the shadow band resulting from 2k(F) spin fluctuations. This band should be detectable experimentally because its intensity is comparable to that of the main band for a large range of momenta.

TI Ferromagnetism in multiband Hubbard models: From weak to strong Coulomb
   repulsion
SO PHYSICAL REVIEW B
LA English
DT Article
ID ELECTRON GROUND-STATES; NAGAOKA STATE; INSTABILITY; LATTICES
AB We propose a mechanism which can lead to ferromagnetism in Hubbard models containing triangles with different on-site energies. It is based on an effective Hamiltonian that we derive in the strong coupling limit. Considering a one-dimensional realization of the model, we show that in the quarter-filled, insulating case the ground state is actually ferromagnetic in a very large parameter range going from Tasaki's flatband limit to the strong coupling limit of the effective Hamiltonian. This result has been obtained using a variety of analytical and numerical techniques. Finally. the same results are shown to apply away from quarter-filling, in the metallic case.

TI Coexistence of different symmetry order parameters near a surface in
   d-wave superconductors .3.
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
DE d-wave superconductor; boundary effect; high-temperature
   superconductivity; time-reversal-breaking state; quasi-classical Green
   function
ID GINZBURG-LANDAU EQUATIONS; VORTEX STRUCTURE; PAIRING STATE;
   DOUBLE-LAYERS; YBA2CU3O7-DELTA; JUNCTIONS; VORTICES; FLUX
AB In previous papers a possibility of coexistence of different symmetry order parameters and their physical. properties have been studied for the (1, 1, 0) surface of d(x)2(-y)2-wave superconductors. The present report extends them to discuss the dependence on the direction of the surface, determining the order parameters self-consistently, For simplicity the surface is assumed to be specular. In the case of a general direction of the surface the symmetry is lower than that for the (1, 1, 0) surface. As a consequence, d(x)2(-y)2 mixes with other symmetry order parameters at the surface. The relative phase between the coexisting order parameters depends on the surface direction; physical properties also change accordingly. Due to the nature of admixture the appearance of the secondary order parameter(s) is possible, even when their couplings are repulsive.

TI Unique carrier properties of neutral lanthanide complex for inorganic
   anions
SO JOURNAL OF MEMBRANE SCIENCE
LA English
DT Article
DE liquid membrane; lanthanide complex; anion transport; anion recognition;
   neutral carrier
ID BOMBARDMENT MASS-SPECTROMETRY; AMINO-ACID; LIQUID MEMBRANE; SELECTIVE
   TRANSPORT; CROWN ETHERS; NUCLEOTIDES; SALTS
AB Lipophilic lanthanide tris(fluorinated P-diketonates) exhibited interesting carrier properties for inorganic anions. Negative FABMS and C-13 NMR studies revealed that they bound small Cl- anion with a large hydration energy more strongly than large Br- and I- anions with small hydration energies. The direct anion coordination features of lanthanide complexes offered unique carrier properties for inorganic anions in liquid membrane transport.

TI Coexistence of different symmetry order parameters near a surface in
   d-wave superconductors .2.
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
DE d-wave superconductor; time-reversal-breaking state; surface current;
   quasi-classical Green function
ID TEMPERATURE-DEPENDENCE; DENSITY; STATES
AB In a previous paper a possibility of coexistence of two superconducting order parameters was discussed for the (1, 1, 0) surface of d(x?2-y?2)-wave superconductors. In the present report physical properties are examined particularly for the time-reversal-breaking stare (s+/-id) near the (1, 1, 0) surface. The nature of coexisting order parameters shows up in the local density of states. It is also shown that the superconducting current flows along the surface due to the time reversal breaking and induces the magnetic field. The induced magnetic field can be used to detect the time-reversal-breaking stares experimentally.

TI KONDO EFFECT DUE TO IMPURITIES WITH (5F)(N) CONFIGURATION - FERMI-LIQUID
   VERSUS NON-FERMI LIQUID
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
DE MULTICHANNEL KONDO MODEL; KONDO EFFECT; NUMERICAL RENORMALIZATION GROUP
   METHOD
ID CONDUCTION ELECTRONS; FIXED-POINT; STABILITY; SINGLET; METALS; STATES
AB The Kondo effect due to U-type impurities is studied in connection with the stability of the Fermi liquid and the non-Fermi liquid. First, an effective exchange Hamiltonian in terms of irreducible tensor operators is derived for conduction electrons, which are coupled with plural 5f electrons. It is based on the assumption of strong spin-orbit and Hund couplings. Second, a model for f(2) configuration placed in a tetragonal or hexagonal crystal held is studied by simplifying the internal structure as the non-Kramers doublet ground slate and the first singlet excited state. The numerical renormalization group analysis shows that the singlet excited state plays an important role to stabilize the Fermi liquid over the non-Fermi liquid. Third, the difference of the Kondo effect is examined between non-Kramers doublet for f(2) and Kramers doublet for f(3) in the presence of the cubic crystal field. It is shown that for f(3) the Hund coupling reduces the channel number to one, while the situation is different for f(2).

TI COEXISTENCE OF DIFFERENT SYMMETRY ORDER PARAMETERS NEAR A SURFACE IN
   D-WAVE SUPERCONDUCTORS .1.
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
DE D-WAVE SUPERCONDUCTOR; COEXISTENCE; DIFFERENT SYMMETRY ORDER PARAMETERS;
   SURFACE EFFECT; TIME-REVERSAL SYMMETRY BREAKING STATE; QUASI-CLASSICAL
   GREEN FUNCTION
ID ANTIFERROMAGNETIC SPIN FLUCTUATIONS; DENSITY; OXIDES; STATES
AB A possible coexistence of different symmetry order parameters is studied near a surface of d-wave supercoductors. The appearance of a different symmetry order parameter depends sensitively on the surface direction relative to the d-wave order parameter. In the case of d(x)2(-y)2-wave, the (1, 1, 0) surface is the most favorable for coexistence. The coexisting order parameters having +/-pi/2 as their relative phase break locally the time-reversal symmetry near the surface.
RP MATSUMOTO, M (reprint author), TOKYO INST TECHNOL, DEPT PHYS, OH OKAYAMA, TOKYO 152, JAPAN.

TI HEXAGONAL ANTIFERROMAGNETS IN STRONG MAGNETIC-FIELD - MAPPING ONTO
   BOSE-CONDENSATION OF LOW-DENSITY BOSE-GAS
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
DE HEXAGONAL ANTIFERROMAGNETS; NONTRIVIAL DEGENERACY; QUANTUM FLUCTUATIONS;
   LOW-DENSITY BOSE GAS; BOSE CONDENSATION; LOW-DENSITY EXPANSION
ID TRIANGULAR LATTICE; HEISENBERG-ANTIFERROMAGNET; QUANTUM FLUCTUATIONS;
   PHASE-TRANSITION; CSCUCL3; MODEL
AB The ground-state spin structures of hexagonal antiferromagnets such as CsCuCl3 in a strong magnetic field are studied by mapping the problem onto an equivalent Bose-gas problem. The spin system close to the saturation is transformed to a low-density Bose gas which has two minima in the single-particle energy band. The low-density expansion is applied to the Bose system and the ground-state spin structure just below saturation field is determined.

TI SPECTRAL-FUNCTION OF THE 1D HUBBARD-MODEL IN THE U-]+INFINITY LIMIT
SO PHYSICAL REVIEW LETTERS
LA English
DT Article
ID TOMONAGA-LUTTINGER MODEL; FERMI GAS; MOMENTUM DISTRIBUTION;
   MAGNETIC-FIELD; PHOTOEMISSION; CONDUCTORS; EXTENSION; EXPONENTS; CHAIN
AB We show that the one-particle spectral functions of the one-dimensional Hubbard model diverge at the Fermi energy like \omega - epsilon(F)\(-3/8) in the U --> + infinity limit. The Luttinger liquid behavior to \omega - epsilon(F)\(alpha), where alpha --> 1/8 as U --> + infinity, should be limited to \omega - epsilon(F)\ similar to t(2)/U (for U large but finite), which shrinks to a single point, omega = epsilon(F), in that limit. The consequences for the observation of the Luttinger liquid behavior in photoemission and inverse photoemission experiments are discussed.
C1 UNIV TOULOUSE 3, PHYS QUANT LAB, F-31062 TOULOUSE, FRANCE.

TI MONOPOLE ACTION AND CONDENSATION IN SU(2) QCD
SO PHYSICS LETTERS B
LA English
DT Article
ID RENORMALIZED COUPLING PARAMETERS; MONTE-CARLO CALCULATION; COLOR
   CONFINEMENT; ABELIAN DOMINANCE; GAUGE-THEORIES; ISING-MODEL; TOPOLOGY
AB An effective monopole action for various extended monopoles is derived from vacuum configurations after abelian projection in the maximally abelian gauge in SU(2) QCD. The action is independent of the lattice volume chosen. Moreover, it depends only on the physical lattice spacing of the renormalized lattice, not on beta. Entropy dominance over the energy of monopole loops is seen on the renormalized lattice with the spacing b>b(c) similar or equal to 5.2x10(-3)Delta(L)(-1). This suggests that monopole condensation always (for all beta) occurs in the infinite-volume limit of lattice QCD.

TI SUPPRESSION OF TRITIUM GAS OXIDATION IN RAT BY NORFLOXACIN AND
   CLINDAMYCIN
SO INTERNATIONAL JOURNAL OF RADIATION BIOLOGY
LA English
DT Article
AB To determine whether intestinal anaerobes are the principal agents responsible for oxidation of tritium gas (HT) in the intestine, the suppressive effects of an antibacterial drug, norfloxacin, and an antibiotic, clindamycin, on tritium uptake in rat exposed to HT were investigated. The administration of norfloxacin or clindamycin to rat was started 1, 2, 3 or 4 days prior to exposure and continued until just before exposure to HT. Following exposure to HT for 2 h, the tritium concentration of tissues and blood was determined. Tritium concentration in blood decreased in proportion to the period of drug administration. In the case of clindamycin, the tritium concentration in the body of the rat decreased to 12% that in control rat. Norfloxacin was less effective than clindamycin. When the administration of clindamycin was begun on the day of exposure and continued for 4 days, the biological half life of urinary tritium in the treated rat was shortened to 53% that in the control rat.
RP ICHIMASA, Y (reprint author), IBARAKI UNIV,FAC SCI,DEPT BIOL,2-1-1 BUNKYO,MITO,IBARAKI 310,JAPAN.

AB Performing a dual transformation numerically, we obtain an effective monopole action from vacuum configurations in compact QED both in the Villain and in the Wilson forms. 1)The DeGrand-Toussaint monopole definition may be useful for beta(v) larger than about 0.5. 2)The Villain model well approximates the Wilson one for beta smaller than beta(c). TI MODEL ANALYSIS OF CURRENT-MODE IMAGES OF HIGHLY ORIENTED
   PYROLYTIC-GRAPHITE BY SCANNING TUNNELING MICROSCOPE IN AIR
SO JAPANESE JOURNAL OF APPLIED PHYSICS PART 1-REGULAR PAPERS SHORT NOTES &
   REVIEW PAPERS
LA English
DT Article
DE STM; HOPG; AIR; ATOMIC CORRUGATION; ELASTIC DEFORMATION; CONTAMINATION
   LAYER
ID BAND STRUCTURE; SURFACE; CORRUGATIONS
AB The current-mode images of highly oriented pyrolytic graphite (HOPG) by scanning tunneling microscope (STM) in air were analyzed in detail by a simple model of the tip and the graphite surface. It was found that the tunneling current is comprised of two components. One is the current through an atom at the top of the tip, which essentially defines the resolution of STM images. The other is the current through the other part of the tip in contact with the sample surface as a result of the elastic deformation of the sample, which becomes dominant in the case of low tunneling resistance. The latter could be explained on the assumption that the tunneling current is proportional to the contact area estimated from the penetration distance of the tip. It was found that the effective tip-sample separation can be modified through the deformation of the intermediate layer on the sample surface.

TI BREAKDOWN OF SELF-INCOMPATIBILITY IN BRASSICA BY THE ANTISENSE RNA OF
   THE SLG GENE
SO PROCEEDINGS OF THE JAPAN ACADEMY SERIES B-PHYSICAL AND BIOLOGICAL
   SCIENCES
LA English
DT Article
DE SELF-INCOMPATIBILITY; BRASSICA; S-LOCUS GLYCOPROTEIN; S-RECEPTOR PROTEIN
   KINASE; TRANSGENIC PLANT; ANTISENSE RNA
ID S-LOCUS GENE; CAMPESTRIS; OLERACEA
AB The self-incompatibility (SI) system of Brassica is sporophytically controlled by multiallenic genes at an S-locus. Two genes, SLG (S-locus glycoprotein) and SRK(S-receptor protein kinase), on the S-locus are thought to play an important role in recognition of the self-pollen, though there is no direct evidence. We introduced the antisense SLG gene to self-incompatible Brassica species through Agrobacterium-mediated transformation. We found that a transgenic plant of B. rapa (syn. B. campestris) could set seeds after self-pollination, and that no SLG protein was detectable in a gel blot analysis of the transgenic plant. These observations provide strong evidence that SLG and/or SRK are directly involved in the pollen-stigma recognition of SI.

TI MONOPOLE ACTION FROM VACUUM CONFIGURATIONS IN COMPACT QED
SO PHYSICS LETTERS B
LA English
DT Article
ID RENORMALIZED COUPLING PARAMETERS; MONTE-CARLO CALCULATION; GAUGE-THEORY;
   ISING-MODEL; CONFINEMENT
AB It is possible to derive a monopole action from vacuum configurations obtained in Monte Carlo simulations extending the method developed by Swendsen. We apply the method to compact QED both in the Villain and in the Wilson forms. The action of the natural monopoles in the Villain case is in fairly good agreement with that derived by the exact dual transformation. Comparing the monopole actions, we find (1) the DeGrand-Toussaint monopole definition may be useful for Pv larger than about 0.5, (2) the Villain model well approximates the Wilson one for beta smaller than beta(c) and (3) in the Wilson action the monopole condensation occurs in the confinement phase and beta(c) may be explained by the energy-entropy balance of monopole loops like in the Villain case.

TI SPIN DYNAMICS AND QUANTUM FLUCTUATIONS IN QUASI-ONE-DIMENSIONAL
   TRIANGULAR ANTIFERROMAGNETS - MAGNETIC-FIELD EFFECTS
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
DE HEISENBERG ANTIFERROMAGNETS; HEXAGONAL LATTICE; CSNICL3; SPIN-WAVE
   THEORY; QUANTUM FLUCTUATIONS; SPIN DYNAMICS; 2-MAGNON EXCITATION
ID EASY-AXIS ANISOTROPY; HALDANE-GAP; HEISENBERG-ANTIFERROMAGNET;
   NEUTRON-SCATTERING; HEXAGONAL ANTIFERROMAGNETS; CSNICL3; EXCITATIONS;
   RESONANCE; RBNICL3; CSMNI3
AB Neutron scattering experiments have revealed that the excitation spectrum in quasione-dimensional ABX(3)-type antiferromagnets, such as CsNiCl3, differs appreciably from the prediction of the conventional linear-spin-wave theory even in the ordered phase. It was shown in a previous paper that the spectrum could be explained well by including two-magnon excitation processes in the spin-wave expansion. Here the theory is extended to study magnetic properties of CsNiCl3 in a magnetic field. The magnetization curve is found to vary with the field nonlinearly with about a half of the classical value. The excitation spectrum is remarkably affected by nonlinear processes. In addition to the effects which are seen at zero field, a hybridization effect and two-magnon peaks in a certain polarization are found to be significant. The results are compared with available experiments and phenomenological theories previously proposed.

TI MONOPOLES AND STRING TENSION IN SU(2) QCD
SO PHYSICS LETTERS B
LA English
DT Article
ID LATTICE GAUGE-THEORY; QUARK CONFINEMENT; COLOR CONFINEMENT; ABELIAN
   DOMINANCE; TOPOLOGY
AB Monopole and photon contributions to abelian Wilson loops are calculated using Monte Carlo simulations of SU(2) QCD in the maximally abelian gauge. The string tension is well reproduced only by monopole contributions, whereas photons alone are responsible for the Coulomb coefficient of the abelian static potential.

TI PROPAGATION LENGTH OF SURFACE-PLASMON POLARITONS PROPAGATING ALONG AIR
   METAL INTERFACE
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
DE SURFACE POLARITON; PROPAGATION LENGTH; METAL FILM; SURFACE ROUGHNESS;
   DIELECTRIC CONSTANT; 2-PRISM METHOD
ID OPTICAL-CONSTANTS; SILVER FILMS; THIN-FILMS; ROUGHNESS
AB We have experimentally measured the propagation length L of surface plasmon polaritons propagating along an air-copper and an air-copper on a CaF2 film interfaces by using a CO2 laser of wavelength 10.6 mum. It is found that the CaF2 film produces a change in the dielectric constant of copper and leads to a decrease of L. It is also shown that L varies with the evaporation speed of the copper film. In order to know the effect of surface roughness on L in the visible region, where various SP experiments have been carried out, we have investigated a roughness effect on the SP propagating along an air-silver interface at wavelength of 0.6328 mum.

TI MONOPOLE CONDENSATION AND CONFINEMENT IN SU(2) QCD
SO NUCLEAR PHYSICS B
LA English
DT Article; Proceedings Paper
CT 1993 International Symposium on Lattice Field Theory (LATTICE 93)
CY OCT 12-16, 1993
CL DALLAS, TX
ID RENORMALIZED COUPLING PARAMETERS; MONTE-CARLO CALCULATION; LATTICE
   GAUGE-THEORIES; COLOR CONFINEMENT; ABELIAN DOMINANCE; QUARK CONFINEMENT;
   ISING-MODEL; TOPOLOGY
AB An effective monopole action is derived from vacuum configurations after abelian projection in the maximally abelian gauge in SU(2) QCD. Entropy dominance over energy of monopole loops is seen on the renormalized lattice with the spacing b > b(c) congruent-to 5.2 x 10(-3)LAMBDA(L)-1 when the physical volume of the system is large enough. Monopole and photon contributions to Wilson loops are calculated also. The string tensions of SU(2) QCD are well reproduced by extended monopole contributions alone.

TI SURFACE-PLASMON POLARITONS IN ATTENUATED TOTAL-REFLECTION GEOMETRY
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
DE ATR GEOMETRY; SURFACE POLARITON; SURFACE MODE; VIRTUAL MODE
AB The dispersion relations of surface polaritons (SP's) with a real frequency and a complex wavenumber in the so-called Otto and Kretschmann geometries have been numerically evaluated. Under a certain condition, SP's fields increase propagating along the surface or increase exponentially going into the prism. It is found that these curious results are induced by the existence of a prism and can be interpreted based on information about electric (or magnetic) fields in the respective layers. Various types of wavenumber, e,g. the wavenumber giving a maximum SP field, are evaluated.

TI DETECTION OF WATER-VAPOR IN T-TAURI STARS
SO ASTROPHYSICAL JOURNAL SUPPLEMENT SERIES
LA English
DT Article
DE CIRCUMSTELLAR MATTER; INFRARED, STARS; MOLECULAR PROCESSES; STARS,
   PRE-MAIN-SEQUENCE
ID MAIN-SEQUENCE STARS; YOUNG STELLAR OBJECTS; ORION MOLECULAR CLOUD;
   FU-ORIONIS; INFRARED OBSERVATIONS; DEUTERATED WATER; CIRCUMSTELLAR
   DISKS; ACCRETION DISKS; H2O ABSORPTION; DARK CLOUDS
AB We have carried out near-infrared spectrophotometry for 52 T Tauri stars in the Taurus-Auriga region in the wavelength range from 0.9 to 2.5 mum. Most of the observed sources show spectral energy distributions flatter than Planck cur-ves. In more than half of our sample, wide and shallow dips due to water vapor are superposed at 1.4 and 1.9 mum on the spectra. After decomposition of the spectra into central star and disk components, the water vapor bands still remain in the disk component. We conclude that water vapor is located in the disk component at least in 17 T Tauri stars (33%) of the sample. The origin of the water vapor is discussed.

TI THEORY OF MAGNETIC-STRUCTURES OF CSCUCL3 IN TRANSVERSE MAGNETIC-FIELD
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
ID TRIANGULAR LATTICE; PHASE-TRANSITION; DEVILS STAIRCASE; ANTIFERROMAGNET;
   MODEL
AB At zero field CsCuCl3 is known to form a helical spin structure along the c-axis and the 120-degrees structure in the c-plane. This paper discusses theoretically the effect of a magnetic field applied perpendicular to the c-axis, which breaks the axial symmetry. First the classical ground state is studied. The transverse magnetic field deforms the helical spin structure and causes a continuous phase transition from the helical (i.e. incommensurate) spin structure to a commensurate state, as the field increases. Detailed studies are made of the helix pitch and of the nature of the inconunensurate spin structure as functions of the field. The commensurate state has a nontrivial degeneracy, which is lifted by quantum (and thermal) fluctuations. Therefore the 1/S expansion is applied to determine the spin structure of the commensurate state. From these studies possible spin structures are suggested for each region of field strength.
RP JACOBS, AE (reprint author), TOKYO INST TECHNOL,DEPT PHYS,OH OKAYAMA,TOKYO 152,JAPAN.

TI NUMERICAL RENORMALIZATION-GROUP STUDY OF MAGNETIC-IMPURITIES IN
   SUPERCONDUCTORS .2. DYNAMICAL EXCITATION-SPECTRA AND SPATIAL VARIATION
   OF THE ORDER-PARAMETER
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
DE MAGNETIC IMPURITY; KONDO EFFECT; SUPERCONDUCTOR; NUMERICAL
   RENORMALIZATION GROUP
AB The Kondo problem in superconductors is studied by extending Wilson's numerical renormalization group method. As a continuation to a previous paper (J. Phys. Soc. Jpn. 61 (1992) 3239), various problems related to the localized excited state produced by a magnetic impurity are examined in detail. In particular, the binding energy of the localized excited state, its spectral weight, one-electron and magnetic excitation spectra and the spatial variation of the order parameter are studied over the whole regime of the magnitude of T(K)/DELTA (T(K): Kondo temperature, DELTA: superconducting energy gap).

TI QUANTUM FLUCTUATIONS AND MAGNETIC-STRUCTURES OF CSCUCL3 IN HIGH
   MAGNETIC-FIELD
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
ID TRIANGULAR LATTICE; PHASE-TRANSITION; ANTIFERROMAGNET; MODEL
AB A theoretical interpretation is given on the magnetization process of CsCuCl3 showing a small jump for the external field applied parallel to the c-axis. It is shown that quantum fluctuations are so important in this S=1/2 triangular antiferromagnet that they can change the ground-state spin structure. The observed magnetization jump is successfully explained as a spin flop process caused by the quantum effect.

TI NONLINEAR EXCITATIONS IN QUASI-ONE-DIMENSIONAL TRIANGULAR
   ANTIFERROMAGNETS
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
ID HALDANE-GAP; HEISENBERG-ANTIFERROMAGNET; NEUTRON-SCATTERING; CSNICL3;
   HELIMAGNETS; TEMPERATURE; DYNAMICS; RBNICL3; SPIN-1; CHAIN
AB Recent neutron experiments have revealed that the excitation spectrum in quasi-one-dimensional ABX3-type antiferromagnets cannot be explained within the conventional linear-spin-wave theory even in the ordered phase. To explain this result, we take into account two-magnon excitation processes in the spin-wave expansion and apply it to CsNiCl3 at T=0. We find that in addition to modifying the energy and intensity of the one-magnon spectrum, these processes can result in large peaks due to two-magnon continuum. The coupling between longitudinal and transverse fluctuations is found to be important as previously suggested by phenomenological Landau-Ginzburg models. Our results agree reasonably well with available experiments. Similar effects can be expected in other quasi-one-dimensional systems having non-collinear spin structures.
RP OHYAMA, T (reprint author), TOKYO INST TECHNOL,DEPT PHYS,OH OKAYAMA,MEGURO KU,TOKYO 152,JAPAN.

TI SURFACE OPTIC WAVES IN ULTRATHIN FILMS BOUNDED BY IDENTICAL SLIGHTLY
   LOSSY MATERIALS
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
ID EXCITON POLARITONS; PRISM; MODES
AB We have investigated the properties of surface optic waves (SOW's), such as surface polaritons or guided waves, in ultrathin films sandwiched by identical slightly lossy materials. It has been found that the imaginary part of dielectric constant Im (epsilon(s)) of surrounding materials strongly affects characteristics of SOW. For example, the propagation length of SOW is remarkably changed by the existence of Im (epsilon(s)).

TI PAIRING AND DEPAIRING EFFECTS OF ANTIFERROMAGNETIC SPIN FLUCTUATIONS IN
   HIGH-TC SUPERCONDUCTIVITY
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
ID NUCLEAR-RELAXATION; NEUTRON-SCATTERING; COPPER OXIDES; OXYGEN SITES;
   YBA2CU3O7; STATES; EXCITATIONS; TRANSITION; DYNAMICS; MODEL
AB The role of antiferromagnetic (AF) spin fluctuations in high-T(c) superconductivity is studied by including both pairing and depairing effects. Thereby the possibility and nature of superconductivity mediated by AF spin fluctuations is examined. Since both of them are based on the same electron system, the superconductivity affects also the AF spin fluctuations as a feedback effect. The present paper discusses this mutual influence to find properties which may be a key to identify experimentally the symmetry of the order parameter.

TI INVESTIGATION OF DISK BENDER LOW-FREQUENCY PROJECTOR WITH DUAL RADIATION
   SURFACES
SO JAPANESE JOURNAL OF APPLIED PHYSICS PART 1-REGULAR PAPERS SHORT NOTES &
   REVIEW PAPERS
LA English
DT Article
DE PROJECTOR; DISK BENDER; LOW-FREQUENCY; HIGH-POWER; MINIATURE; LIGHT
   WEIGHT; FEM ANALYSIS; EQUIVALENT CIRCUIT
AB A low-frequency disk bender projector with dual radiation surfaces was designed on the basis of finite element method (FEM) analysis and equivalent circuit analysis, in order to devise a miniature light weight projector with a high sound pressure level. These analyses suggest that a low-frequency, high-power, miniature and light weight projector can be realized. A trial projector was produced and evaluated. The resonant frequencies for the projector in air and water were 1315 Hz and 970 Hz, respectively. Experimental maximum transmitting voltage sensitivity was 132.2 dB re 1 muPa/V at 1 m.

TI NUMERICAL RENORMALIZATION-GROUP STUDY OF THE KONDO EFFECT IN
   SUPERCONDUCTORS
SO PHYSICA B-CONDENSED MATTER
LA English
DT Article
AB The numerical renormalization group method is applied to study a magnetic impurity in a superconductor. The ground state and the first excited state, which are either a doublet (S = 1/2) or a singlet (S = 0), are traced with the renormalization step. The position and the spectral weight of the localized excited state within the energy gap are determined as a function of T(K)/DELTA (T(K) Kondo temperature, DELTA = superconducting energy gap). The present theory gives a reliable description for the whole region of T(K)/DELTA.

TI AN INFRARED STUDY OF HOT DUST IN QUASARS USING PRISM SPECTROPHOTOMETRY
SO ASTROPHYSICAL JOURNAL
LA English
DT Article
DE GALAXIES, ISM; GALAXIES, NUCLEI; GALAXIES, PHOTOMETRY; INFRARED,
   GALAXIES; QUASARS, GENERAL; RADIATION MECHANISMS, THERMAL
ID CONTINUUM ENERGY-DISTRIBUTIONS; COLOR-SELECTED QUASARS; SEYFERT-1
   GALAXIES; OPTICAL-PROPERTIES; SILICATE GRAINS; MICRONS; VARIABILITY;
   GRAPHITE
AB Low-resolution near-infrared spectra were obtained for 14 quasars with redshift z < 0.3. The observed continua from 0.95 to 2.5 mum were reproduced remarkably well with a combination of two radiation components, i.e., the power law and the blackbody radiation which are, respectively, dominated at shorter than approximately 1.2 mum and longer than approximately 1.5 mum. The longer part of the spectra fit a single-temperature blackbody of 1470 +/- 90 K which is attributable to the thermal emission from hot dust grains heated by the central power source. The flux ratio of the blackbody of the power-law component ranges by a factor of 6. It was found that an IRAS color selected sample tended to have a larger flux ratio as compared to non-IRAS quasars.

TI A STATIC BARYON IN A DUAL ABELIAN EFFECTIVE THEORY OF QCD
SO NUCLEAR PHYSICS B
LA English
DT Article
ID QUARK CONFINEMENT; POTENTIAL MODELS; MECHANISM; MASSES; MESONS
AB The potential of a static baryon is studied numerically in a dual abelian effective theory of QCD. The Dirac quantization condition forbids DELTA-type flux. Minimizing the vacuum energy with respect to various flux distributions, we find that a baryon carries Y- or LAMBDA-type flux according to the configuration of the quarks. The flux is squeezed as expected when monopole condensation occurs. The potential evaluated is slightly different from that usually assumed as the summation of the two-body potentials.

TI EFFECTIVE HAMILTONIAN AND PHASE-TRANSITIONS OF HEXAGONAL HEISENBERG
   ANTIFERROMAGNETS WITH EASY-AXIS ANISOTROPY
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
ID TRIANGULAR-LATTICE; ORDERED PHASES; MAGNETIC-STRUCTURES; SCALING
   ANALYSIS; ISING-MODEL; CSNICL3; CSMNI3; RENORMALIZATION; BEHAVIOR;
   CSNIBR3
AB A detailed study is made on Heisenberg antiferromagnets on the hexagonal lattice such as CsNiCl3 or CsMnI3, which have an easy-axis anisotropy. First, an effective Hamiltonian is derived for low-energy fluctuations of local 120-degrees spin structure. Then, Monte Carlo simulations are carried out with this Hamiltonian to study in detail the nature of phase transitions and their critical properties. Two successive phase transitions are detected; estimated critical exponents for two phase transitions turn out to be consistent with the universality class of three-dimensional XY model. A very gradual increase of uniform magnetization is also observed below the upper transition temperature T(N1). From a consideration with finite-size scaling theory, we conclude that only the cosine-mode is chosen below T(N1).

SO ASTROPHYSICAL JOURNAL

   CORES; IRS-5
AB Water vapor absorption features were detected at 1.4 and 1.9 mum in all the six observed objects; four FU Orionis variables (FU Ori, V1515 Cyg, V1057 Cyg, and Elias 1-12) and two related objects (L1551 IRS 5 and Z CMa). We discuss the idea that the water vapor appears by vaporization of ice or crystalline water in the grains or rocks accreting from the outer and cooler regions of a disk surrounding T Tauri stars, in conjunction with the flare-up of the FU Orionis variables.

TI A NEAR-INFRARED PRISM SPECTROPHOTOPOLARIMETER
SO PUBLICATIONS OF THE ASTRONOMICAL SOCIETY OF THE PACIFIC
LA English
DT Article
AB A 16-channel, prism spectrophotopolarimeter (PSP) is described. It covers the near-infrared spectral region from 0.9 to 2.5 mum including the standard, I, J, H, and K bands, with a resolution of approximately 0.1 mum. This spectrometer employs cooled field optics in order to alleviate wavelength shifts caused by differences of image positions in the diaphragm. The field optics, in cooperation with the simultaneity owing to the 16-channel linear array ( 15 InSbs plus a single Si detector), enable us to achieve polarimetric accuracies as high as 0.2%. PSP is capable of quick conversion between photometric and polarimetric modes by inserting or retracting a half-wave plate and a wiregrid polarizer in the optics. The detection limits of the photometric mode at the UH 2.2-m telescope atop Mauna Kea are 13.0, 12.6, 12.7, and 11.7 mag/square-root HZ at the wavelength corresponding to the 0.94 (i), 1.18 (j), 1.62 (h), and 2.13 (k) band centers, respectively. Example of the observed data are presented.

TI NUMERICAL RENORMALIZATION-GROUP STUDY OF MAGNETIC-IMPURITIES IN
   SUPERCONDUCTORS
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
ID ANDERSON MODEL; KONDO PROBLEM; STATIC PROPERTIES; ALLOYS
AB A magnetic impurity doped in a superconductor produces a localized excited state within the energy gap. This problem is studied by applying Wilson's numerical renormalization group method. The ground state and the first excited state are traced by changing the exchange coupling constant relative to the energy gap. Thereby the position of the localized excited state within the energy gap is determined over the whole regime of the magnitude of T(K)/DELTA (T(K): Kondo temperature, DELTA: superconducting energy gap). A crossing of the lowest doublet and singlet is clearly observed at T(K)/DELTA congruent-to 0.3. The ferromagnetic and Ising cases have been studied also. In the ferromagnetic case the localized excited state stays close to the gap edge since the exchange coupling is renormalized to a weak coupling. The case of the Ising-like sd coupling, which is exactly solvable, can be used to check the reliability of the present approach and the effect of the discretization.
C1 TOHOKU UNIV,DEPT PHYS,SENDAI,MIYAGI 980,JAPAN.

TI STUDIES ON SURFACE-POLARITONS IN ULTRATHIN FILMS SANDWICHED BY IDENTICAL
   DIELECTRICS
SO JOURNAL OF THE PHYSICAL SOCIETY OF JAPAN
LA English
DT Article
ID EXCITON POLARITONS; MODES; SILVER; PRISM
AB We have investigated the spatial distribution of electric and magnetic fields and propagation characteristics of surface polaritons in ultrathin films with the thickness of less than 10 nm. The long-range surface polariton configuration, such as the dielectric/ultrathin film/dielectric geometry, was employed. For Ag thin film, the propagation lengths have been calculated by using effective dielectric constants evaluated from experiments or by a semi-empirical method. The propagation length monotonically increases with decreasing the thickness of Ag film. We have found that there is a sharp resonance in attenuated total reflection (ATR) spectra even for a s-polarized light.

TI SUPERCONDUCTING CORRELATIONS IN THE ONE-DIMENSIONAL T-J MODEL
SO PHYSICAL REVIEW B
LA English
DT Article
ID HUBBARD-MODEL; SYSTEMS; SEPARATION; EXPONENTS; BAND; SPIN
AB The t-J model is the simplest Hamiltonian for strongly correlated electrons, in which a superconducting phase may be present. This paper discusses superconducting correlation functions of the one-dimensional t-J model obtained from exact diagonalization of finite systems. Singlet and triplet channels are examined and compared with each other; the results are interpreted in terms of the Luttinger-liquid theory. A detailed study is made of the small-J limit, where the special form of the ground-state wave function allows a thorough study of correlation functions, including logarithmic corrections to the leading power-law decay. In addition, the effect of a magnetic field is also examined, since singlet and triplet superconducting correlations are competitive at zero field. It turns out that the magnetic field modifies the superconducting correlations in an interesting way. In particular, an analog of the Fulde-Ferrell state is found for some intermediate J.
RP PRUSCHKE, T (reprint author), TOKYO INST TECHNOL,DEPT PHYS,TOKYO 152,JAPAN.

TI OBSERVATION OF SURFACE CORRUGATION OF HIGHLY ORIENTED PYROLYTIC-GRAPHITE
   BY SCANNING TUNNELING MICROSCOPE IN AIR
SO JAPANESE JOURNAL OF APPLIED PHYSICS PART 1-REGULAR PAPERS SHORT NOTES &
   REVIEW PAPERS
LA English
DT Article
DE STM; HOPG SURFACE; AIR; ATOMIC CORRUGATION
ID MOLECULES; DNA
AB The apparent surface corrugation of highly oriented pyrolytic graphite (HOPG) was investigated with a scanning tunneling microscope (STM) in air using mechanically polished PtIr tips. It was found that the tunneling resistance was the most dominant parameter governing the observed atomic corrugation. The tunneling resistance was defined by the ratio of bias voltage to tunneling current required for STM measurements. The maximum corrugation of about 0.3 nm was attained at the tunneling resistance around 10(7) OMEGA. The dependence of the corrugation upon tunneling resistance is qualitatively explained taking into account the variation of tip function, by means of both the elastic deformation of the sample surface and the separation change of the tip and surface.
RP IRI, T (reprint author), UNIV ELECTROCOMMUN,CHOFU,TOKYO 182,JAPAN.

TI PAIRING CORRELATIONS FOR THE 1-DIMENSIONAL T-J MODEL
SO PHYSICA C
LA English
DT Article; Proceedings Paper
CT INTERNATIONAL CONF ON MATERIALS AND MECHANISMS OF SUPERCONDUCTIVITY HIGH
   TEMPERATURE SUPERCONDUCTORS 3
CY JUL 22-26, 1991
CL KANAZAWA, JAPAN
AB We present results for singlet and triplet pairing correlation functions of the one dimensional t-J model obtained via exact diagonalization of finite systems.  The general behavior found supports the predictions by the Luttinger liquid picture, especially a size analysis of the critical behavior near k = 0 gives the same critical exponents for both correlation functions.  The relative magnitude of the singlet pairing correlations to the triplet ones is examined in this connection.  In addition, the magnetic field effect on the pairing correlations is also studied.
RP PRUSCHKE, T (reprint author), TOKYO INST TECHNOL,DEPT PHYS,MEGURO KU,TOKYO 152,JAPAN.

TI CORRELATION-FUNCTIONS AND CRITICAL EXPONENTS IN THE ONE-DIMENSIONAL
   ANISOTROPIC T-J MODEL
SO PHYSICAL REVIEW B
LA English
DT Article
ID SPIN-CORRELATION; HUBBARD-MODEL; MONTE-CARLO; SUPERCONDUCTIVITY;
   SYSTEMS; BEHAVIOR; CHAINS; BAND; GAS
AB The momentum distribution and the spin-correlation functions are studied for the one-dimensional t-J model, in which the exchange interaction J is anisotropic. The discussion is focused on the nontrivial limit that J is much smaller than t. In this limit the exact ground-state wave function is a product of the spinless-fermion Slater determinant and the spin-wave function of the s = 1/2 anisotropic Heisenberg antiferromagnet. With this wave function, correlation functions are calculated explicitly for finite but large systems and the nature of their singularities is studied. It is found that for the XY-like anisotropy the critical behavior of correlation functions can be described by the Tomonaga-Luttinger model, while for the Ising-like anisotropy the model seems to belong to the universality class of the Luther-Emery model of the one-dimensional electron gas.
RP PRUSCHKE, T (reprint author), TOKYO INST TECHNOL,DEPT PHYS,O OKAYAMA,MEGURO KU,TOKYO 152,JAPAN.

TI MAGNETIC-FIELD EFFECTS ON THE CORRELATION-FUNCTIONS IN THE
   ONE-DIMENSIONAL STRONGLY CORRELATED HUBBARD-MODEL
SO PHYSICAL REVIEW B
LA English
DT Article
ID TEMPERATURE; LIQUID; STATE
AB The momentum distribution function and spin-correlation functions are studied for the one-dimensional large-U Hubbard model with an emphasis on the effects of the magnetic field.  A direct calculation of the correlation functions is carried out with the exact wave function, whose explicit form for the large-U limit was derived in a previous paper.  Singularities are detected at K(F-sigma) and K(F-sigma) + 2K(F-sigma) in the momentum distribution function n-sigma(k), where K(F-sigma) is the Fermi wave number of the noninteracting electrons with a given magnetization.  Similarly, the longitudinal spin-correlatio function S(zz)(k) has singularities at 2K(F-up) and K(F-down), while the transverse one S(xx)(K) is singular at K(F-up) + K(F-down) and K(F-up) - K(F-down).  The nature of the singularities (i.e., critical exponents) is the singularities (i.e., critical exponents) is determined determined from an analysis of the size dependence.  As a complementary approach, those critical exponents for the U/t --> infinity limit are explicitly calculated with conformal field theory.  In this limit the exponents depends only on the magnetization and are independent of the electron density.  The resulting exponents are consistent with the first results.
C1 TOKYO INST TECHNOL,DEPT PHYS,TOKYO 152,JAPAN.

TI CORRELATION-FUNCTIONS IN 1-DIMENSIONAL LARGE-U HUBBARD-MODEL -
   ZERO-FIELD AND FINITE-FIELD CASES
SO INTERNATIONAL JOURNAL OF MODERN PHYSICS B
LA English
DT Article
AB A recent study of the large-U limit of the one-dimensional (1D) Hubbard model is presented and discussed.  It is pointed out first that the wave function has a simple structure in this limit.  Namely, it is a product of Slater determinant of non-interacting spinless fermions and the wave function of 1D S = 1/2 Heisenberg antiferromagnet.  Secondly, by using this property, a direct calculation of momentum distribution and spin correlation function is carried out for the ground state at zero-field and finite-field cases.  The results show various singularities exactly at the same position where one expects for the small-U case in both zero-field and finite-field cases.  The critical exponents estimated from the size dependence are in reasonable agreement with those predicted by the Tomonaga-Luttinger-liquid and the conformal field theory.
RP SHIBA, H (reprint author), TOKYO INST TECHNOL,DEPT PHYS,TOKYO 152,JAPAN.

TI VARIATIONAL THEORY OF CORRELATED FERMI-LIQUID STATE IN THE KONDO LATTICE
   MODEL
SO INTERNATIONAL JOURNAL OF MODERN PHYSICS B
LA English
DT Article
AB A variational wave function is constructed and studied for the spin-compensated Fermi-liquid-type ground state in the Kondo lattice model.  The spins of the localized f-electrons are compensated by overlapping conduction-electron clouds.  In accordance with Luttinger's theorem, the volume enclosed by the Fermi surface corresponds to the total number of electrons, i.e., it includes the f-electrons as well as the conduction electrons.  An approximate analytic treatment of the correlated heavy Fermi liquid is given by using the Gutzwiller approximation.
RP FAZEKAS, P (reprint author), UNIV COLOGNE,INST THEORET PHYS,ZULPICHER STR 77,W-5000 COLOGNE 41,GERMANY.

AB A report is made on recent studies of the spin correlation function and the momentum distribution function in the one-dimensional large-U Hubbard model. TI CORRELATED FERMI-LIQUID STATE FORMED WITH OVERLAPPING KONDO CLOUDS - A
   VARIATIONAL STUDY
SO PROGRESS OF THEORETICAL PHYSICS SUPPLEMENT
LA English
DT Article
ID PERIODIC ANDERSON MODEL; GROUND-STATE; GUTZWILLER METHOD; MONTE-CARLO;
   HIGH DIMENSIONS; VALENCE; WAVEFUNCTION; ELECTRONS
AB A simple variational description is given on the nature of overlapping Kondo clouds, which compensate the localized f-spins in the Kondo lattice.  It is shown explicity that the f-electrons participate in forming a "large Fermi surface", although they are strictly localized.  The resulting correlated Fermi liquid, i.e., heavy fermions, is examined with the variational Monte Carlo method and is compared with the Gutzwiller approximation.  The relation to the periodic Anderson model is also discussed in this connection.
